Whitney anukramaс╣З─л

[Atharvan.тАФtrayaс╕е pary─Бy─Бс╕е.]

Whitney

Comment

тМКProse, except vss. 19-22.тМЛ A corresponding passage is found in P─Бipp. xvi., but so different in detail that it would require to be given in full for comparison; and this has not been done.

SPP., without any good reason,* counts the three pary─Бyas or divisions of this hymn as so many independent hymns, thus not only defacing the structure of the book, but defeating all the references that had been made to it in lexicons and elsewhere.

*тМКWhether Whitney’s condemnation of SPP’s procedure is justified or not may be decided when all the facts are before us. Some of them have been put together by me, above, pages 610, 611, which see.тМЛ

тМКThe hymn is not cited by V─Бit.; nor in the text of K─Бu┼Ы., unless vs. 31 is meant at 62. 8: but Ke┼Ыava (p. 3531) cites it for use in witchcraft practices (so the comm.), and also (p. 3652) for use in the bс╣Ыhaspati sava (so comm.).тМЛ

Translations

Translated: Henry, 106, 145; Griffith, ii. 61.тАФCf. especially Henry’s introduction, p. 145. The rice-dish, hot and yellow and nourishing, is a symbol of the sun (cf. vs. 50); its ingredients and the utensils used in making it are identified with all sorts of things in the most grotesque manner of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas.

Griffith

A glorification of the Odana or oblation of boiled rice

Translation
  1. The theologues (brahmav─Бd├нn) say: hast thou eaten (pra-a┼Ы) the
    rice-dish as it was retiring (p├бr─Б├▒c), or as it was coming on
    (praty├б├▒c)?
Notes

The pluta- or protracted syllables in this and the next verse are
quoted in Pr─Бt. i. 105, but nothing is said as to their accentuation,
from which it seems most plausible to infer that the protraction made no
difference in the accent; and though in the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas a protracted
syllable is always accented тМКsee Gram. ┬з78 aтМЛ, that is not the
invariable rule in the Vedic texts (thus, only once among the three
instances occurring in RV.). Here the mss. are greatly at variance.
тМКSPP’s V. (a then living ┼Ыrotriya) read pr─Б╠Б┼Ы─л╠Б3с╕е; and by his ms.
D^(c) the reading pr─Б╠Б┼Ы─л╠Бс╕е3 is given secunda manu. Among our mss.,
O.R.Kp. (and E.?) give pr─Б╠Б┼Ы─л╠Бс╕е3. SPP. reports that 16 of his
authorities agree in giving praty├б├▒c─Б╠Б3m; and (apart from the presence
or position of the 3) this seems to be the reading of many of W’s
mss.тМЛ SPP’s text gives an accent to the protracted syllable in both
cases in both vs. 26 and vs. 27.тАФтМКSPP’s pada-reading in vs. 26 is
pr├б: ─Б┼Ы─л╠Б3с╕е, and in 27 it is pr├б: ─Б╠Б┼Ы─л╠Б3с╕е. An accented ─Б╠Б in ─Б┼Ы─л╠Б3с╕е
would require praре░─Б╠Б┼Ы─л╠Б3с╕е (cf. vs. 28); but one does not see why the ─Б
should be accented.тМЛ

The theologians say, Thou hast eaten the averted Odana and the Odana turned hither- ward.

Translation
  1. The rice-dish itself hath eaten the rice-dish.
Notes

[Pary─Бya II.тАФdv─Бsaptati. mantroktadevatyam. a, of 32, 38,
41, g of 32-49. s─Бmn─л triс╣гс╣нubh; b of 32, 35, 42, c
32-49, e of 33, 34, 44-48, 1-p. ─Бsur─л g─Бyatr─л; d of 32, 41,
43, 47. d─Бiv─л jagat─л; b of 38, 44, 46, e of 32, 33-43, 49.
1-p. ─Бsury anuс╣гс╣нubh; f of 32-49. s─Бmny anuс╣гс╣нubh; a of
33-49.* ─Бrcy anuс╣гс╣нubh; a of 37. s─Бmn─л pan╠Дkti; b of 33, 36,
40, 47, 48. ─Бsur─л jagat─л; b of 34, 37, 41, 43, 45. ─Бsur─л pan╠Дkti;
d of 34. ─Бsur─л triс╣гс╣нubh; d of 35, 46, 48. y─Бjuс╣г─л g─Бyatr─л;
d of 36, 37, 40. d─Бivi pan╠Дkti; d of 38, 39. pr─Бj─Бpaty─Б
g─Бyatr─л; b of 39. ─Бsury uс╣гс╣Зih; d of 42, 45, 49, d─Бivi
triс╣гс╣нubh; b of 49. 1-p. bhurik s─Бmn─л bс╣Ыhat─л.тАа]

*тМКThe text of the Anukr. reads enam any─Бbhy─Бс╣Б ┼Ыrotr─Бbhy─Бm (= a of
33) ity ─Бditaс╕е saptada┼Ы─Б тАЭrcyanuс╣гс╣нubhaс╕е. The definition applies (perhaps
with occasional forcing) to 14 of the 17 first avas─Бnas of vss. 33-49.
As for the other 3, the a of 38 and the a of 41 are accurately
defined above, in the first line of the Anukr. excerpts for this
pary─Бya; and the a of 37, in the definition next following the
asterisk.тМЛ

тАатМКThe definition of 33 d, 44 d (9 syllables) is omitted by the
Anukr.тМЛ

The second pary─Бya of this hymn is reckoned in the Anukr. as of 72
divisions in 18 gaс╣Зas or paragraphs; but the actual division in the
mss. is into 126 such divisions (7 to each gaс╣Зa), as given in both
editions; and the metrical description of the Anukr. (as reported above)
is also on that basis.

тМКThe division of this pary─Бya into 72 avas─Бnas.тАФIn his Critical
Notice, p. 20-21, at the beginning of his first volume, SPP. treats of
this matter; and just after the end (p. 356) of the text of his third
volume, he prints again this pary─Бya, but divided into 72 avas─Бnas
“according to the instructions contained in the Sarv─Бnukramaс╣Зik─Б” which
he had printed in the Critical Notice, l.c.тМЛ

тМКThe Major Anukr. calls the 18 main divisions of this pary─Бya
(answering to the “verses” of the Berlin ed.) by the name of daс╣Зс╕Нakas.
Since the daс╣Зс╕Нakas are all subdivided, they are also (see p. 472)
called ganas. Each dandaka falls into 7 subdivisions or avas─Бnas,
which may be designated as a, b, c, d, e, f, g. Each of these 7 is
written out and counted for the first and last daс╣Зс╕Нaka (vss. 32 and
49, Berlin).тМЛ

тМКSimilarly, in a sequence of refrains or anuс╣гan╠Дgas, the refrain is
given and counted as an avas─Бna only for its first and last occurrence
in that sequence. The third subdivision (or c: beginning taс╣Б v─Б
aham) of each daс╣Зс╕Нaka, being unvaried throughout the pary─Бya,
constitutes a sequence of 18 and is given and counted independently only
for vss. 32 and 49; while for the 16 vss., 33-48, it is given (see SPP.
in vol. iii.) and counted as one with b, thus making the avas─Бna
to consist of b-c.тАФIn like manner, the sixth subdivision (or f:
beginning eс╣гa v─Б odanaс╕е) and the seventh subdivision (or g:
beginning sarv─Бn╠Дga eva), being unvaried throughout, constitute a
sequence of 18 and are given and counted independently only for vss. 32
and 49; while for the other 16 vss. they are counted as one with e,
thus making the avas─Бna to consist of e-g.тМЛ

тМКFurthermore, and on the other hand, subdivision e varies as to its
beginning between ten─Бi тАЩnam, tay─Бi тАЩnam, and t─Бir enam, and
t─Бbhy─Бm enam: but we find no unvaried sequences of more than two
except ten─Бi тАЩnam etc. in the 5 vss., 39-43, and t─Бbhy─Бm enam
etc. in the 5 vss., 44-48. For vss. 40, 41, 42, accordingly, and for
vss. 45, 46, 47, as well, not only is f-g reckoned to e, but
also e-f-g is reckoned as an anuс╣гan╠Дga to d, thus making the
avas─Бna to consist of d-g.тМЛ

тМКFor these six verses, therefore, arranged and counted as 3 avas─Бnas
(a, b-c, d-g), we have the reckoning 6 ├Ч 3 = 18.тАФFor verses 32 and
49 (counted as a, b, c, d, e, f, g, as above noted), we have the
reckoning 2 ├Ч 7 = 14.тАФAnd for the remaining ten verses, we have the
arrangement and count, a, b-c, d, e-g, or 10 ├Ч 4 = 40. This gives us
(18 + 14 + 40 =) 72, which is the count, not only of the Major Anukr.,
but of the Old Anukr. or Pa├▒capaс╣нalik─Б. as well.тМЛ

рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛реСрдЩреНрдЧ рдПреТрд╡ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реСрдкрд░реБрдГреТ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реСрддрдиреВрдГреТ рд╕рдВ рднреСрд╡рддрд┐реТ рдп рдПреТрд╡рдВ рд╡реЗрджреС рее

рейреи рддрддрд╢реНрдЪреИрдирдордиреНрдпреЗрди рд╢реАрд░реНрд╖реНрдгрд╛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. If тМКcaтМЛ thou hast eaten it with another head than that (t├бtas)
    with which the ancient seers ate this, thy progeny, from the oldest
    down, will die: so one says to him; it verily I [have] not [eaten]
    coming hither (arv─Б╠Б├▒c), nor retiring, nor coming on; with Brihaspati
    [as] head, therewith have I eaten it, therewith have I made it go;
    this rice-dish, verily, is whole-limbed, whole-jointed, whole-bodied;
    whole-limbed, whole-jointed, whole-bodied becometh he who knoweth thus.
Notes

The pada-reading of pr─Б╠Б┼Ы─лs in a is praре░─Б╠Б┼Ы─лс╕е.

Griffith

And thence he said to this one, Thou hast eaten this with a different head from that with which the ancient Rishis ate: thy offspring, reckoning from the eldest, will die. I have eaten it neither turned downward, nor turned away, nor turned hitherward. With Brihaspati as head: with him I have eaten, with him have I come to it. Now this Odana is complete with all members, joints, and body. Complete, verily, with all his members, joints, and body is he who possess this knowledge.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If thou hast eaten it with other ears than those тМКt├бtasтМЛ with
    which the ancient seers ate this, thou wilt become deaf: thus one says
    to him; it verily [have] I not [eaten] coming hither, nor retiring,
    nor coming on; with heaven-and-earth as ears, with them have I eaten it,
    with them have I made it go etc. etc.
Notes
Griffith

And thence he said to him, Thou hast eaten this with other ears than those with which the ancient Rishis ate it. Thou wilt be deaf. I have eaten it neither, etc. (as in verse 32). With Heaven and Earth as ears, with these I have eaten it, with these I have come to it. Now this Odana, etc. (as in 32).

Whitney
Translation
  1. If thou hast eaten it with other eyes than those with which the
    ancient seers ate this, thou wilt become blind: thus one says to him; it
    verily [have] I not [eaten] coming hither, nor retiring, nor coming
    on; with sun-and-moon as eyes, with them have I eaten it, with them etc.
    etc.
Notes

All the mss. read s┼лry─Бcandramas─Б╠Бbhy─Бm, which SPP. has very properly
retained in his text; ours was altered to agree with vi. 128. 3, but the
alteration should have been the other way.

Griffith

And thence he said to him. Thou hast eaten this with other eyes . . . thou wilt be blind. With Sun and Moon, etc.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If thou hast eaten it with another mouth (m├║kha) than that with
    which the ancient seers ate this, thy progeny will die from in front
    (mukhat├бs): thus one says to him; it verily [have] I not [eaten]
    coming hither, nor retiring, nor coming on; with br├бhman as mouth,
    therewith have I etc. etc.
Notes
Griffith

And thence, etc. . . with other month. Thy offspring will die, reckoning from the head . . . With Brahma as mouth.

рейрем рддрддрд╢реНрдЪреИрдирдордиреНрдпрдпрд╛ рдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рдпрд╛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. If thou hast eaten it with another tongue than that with which the
    ancient seers ate this, thy tongue will die: thus one says to him; it
    verily [have] I not [eaten] coming hither, nor retiring, nor coming
    on; with Agni’s tongue, therewith have I etc. etc.
Notes
Griffith

And thence, etc. . . . with other tongue . . . Thy tongue will die . . . With the tongue of Agni.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If thou hast eaten it with other teeth than those with which the
    ancient seers ate this, thy teeth will fall out (┼Ыad): thus one says
    to him; it verily [have] I not [eaten] coming hither, nor retiring,
    nor coming on; with the seasons as teeth, therewith have I etc. etc.
Notes

The comm. reads satsyanti for ┼Ыatsyanti.

Griffith

And thence, etc. . . With other teeth . . . Thy teeth will fall out . . . With the Seasons as teeth.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If thou hast eaten it with other breaths-and-expirations than those
    with which the ancient seers ate this, breaths-and-expirations will quit
    thee: thus one says to him; it verily [have] I not [eaten] coming
    hither, nor retiring, nor coming on; with the seven seers as
    breaths-and-expirations, therewith have I etc. etc.
Notes

The mss., as usual, are divided between saptarс╣гibhis and saptaс╣Ыс╣гi-
in this verse; SPP. adopts the former.

Griffith

And thence, etc. . . . with other vital airs. . . . Thy vital airs will leave thee . . . With the Seven Rishis as the vital airs.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If thou hast eaten it with another bulk (vy├бcas) than that with
    which the ancient seers ate this, the king-y├бkshma will slay thee:
    thus one says to him; it verily [have] I not [eaten] coming hither,
    nor retiring, nor coming on; with the atmosphere as bulk, therewith have
    I etc. etc.
Notes

The comm. explains vyacas─Б by vy─Бptimat─Б r┼лpeс╣Зa.

Griffith

And thence, etc. . . . with other expanse . . . Consumption will destroy thee . . . With the firmament as expanse.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If thou hast eaten it with another back than that with which the
    ancient seers ate this, the lightning will slay thee: thus one says to
    him; it verily [have] I not [eaten] coming hither, nor retiring, nor
    coming on; with the sky as back, therewith have I etc. etc.
Notes
Griffith

And thence, etc. . . . with other back. . . . Lightning will slay thee. . . With the heaven as back.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If thou hast eaten it with another breast than that with which the
    ancient seers ate this, thou wilt not prosper with plowing: thus one
    says to him; it verily [have] I not [eaten] coming hither, nor
    retiring, nor coming on; with the earth as breast, therewith have I etc.
    etc.
Notes
Griffith

And thence, etc. . . . with other breast . . . Thou wilt fail in agriculture. . . . With the earth as breast.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If thou hast eaten it with another belly than that with which the
    ancient seers ate this, the colic (? udarad─Бr├б) will slay thee: thus
    one says to him; it verily [have] I not [eaten] coming hither, nor
    retiring, nor coming on; with truth as belly, therewith have I etc. etc.
Notes

The comm. explains udarad─Бra as udarasya daraс╣З─Бtmako тАЩt─лs─Бr─Бkhyo
rogaс╕е, or diarrh┼Уa.

Griffith

And thence, etc. . . . with other belly . . . colic will destroy thee . . . With truth as belly.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If thou hast eaten it with another bladder than that with which the
    ancient seers ate this, thou wilt die in the waters: thus one says to
    him; it verily [have] I not [eaten] coming hither, nor retiring, nor
    coming on; with the ocean as bladder, therewith have I etc. etc.
Notes
Griffith

And thence, etc. . . . with other abdomen . . . Thou wilt die in the water . . . With the sea as abdomen.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If thou hast eaten it with other thighs than those with which the
    ancient seers ate this, thy thighs will die: thus one says to him; it
    verily [have] I not [eaten] coming hither, nor retiring, nor coming
    on; with the thighs of Mitra-and-Varuс╣Зa, therewith have I etc. etc.
Notes
Griffith

And thence, etc. . . . with other thighs . . . Thy thigh will perish . . . With Mitra-Varuna as thighs.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If thou hast eaten it with other knees (aс╣гс╣нh─лv├бnt) than those
    with which the ancient seers ate this, thou wilt become lame: thus one
    says to him; it verily [have] I not [eaten] coming hither, nor
    retiring, nor coming on; with Tvashс╣нar’s knees, therewith have I etc.
    etc.
Notes
Griffith

And thence, etc. . . . with other knees . . . Thou wilt become a sick man . . . With the knees of Tvashtar.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If thou hast eaten it with other feet than those with which the
    ancient seers ate this, thou wilt be much-wandering: thus one says to
    him; it verily [have] I not [eaten] coming hither, nor retiring,
    nor coming on; with the feet of the two A┼Ыvins, therewith have I etc.
    etc.
Notes
Griffith

And thence, etc. . . . with other feet . . . Thou wilt become a wanderer . . . With the feet of the Asvins.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If thou hast eaten it with other front-feet than those with which
    the ancient seers ate this, a serpent will slay thee: thus one says to
    him; it verily [have] I not [eaten] coming hither, nor retiring, nor
    coming on; with Savitar’s front-feet, therewith have I etc. etc.
Notes

Read in our text savit├║с╕е in d (an accent-mark slipped out of
place).

Griffith

And thence, etc. . . with other fore-parts of the feet . . . A serpent will kill thee . . . With the fore-parts of Savitar’s feet.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If thou hast eaten it with other hands than those with which the
    ancient seers ate this, thou wilt slay a Brahman: thus one says to him;
    it verily [have] I not [eaten] coming hither, nor retiring, nor
    coming on; with the hands of righteousness (с╣Ыt├б), therewith have I
    etc. etc.
Notes
Griffith

And thence, etc. . . . with other hands . . . The Brahmana (divine power) will kill thee . . . With the hands of Right.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If thou hast eaten it with another firm standing (pratiс╣гс╣нh─Б╠Б) than
    that with which the ancient seers ate this, without firm standing,
    without support (─Бy├бtana) wilt thou die: thus one says to him; it
    verily [have] I not [eaten] coming hither, nor retiring, nor coming
    on; standing firm in truth, therewith have I etc. etc.
Notes

All our saс╣Бhit─Б-mss., and the majority of SPP’s, have the false accent
apratiс╣гс╣нh─Бn├│ тАШn─Бy- in b; both editions emend to -с╣гс╣нh─Бn├▓. Some of
our mss. (B.P.M.) read pratiс╣гс╣нh─Б╠Бy─Б in d, as if aiming at
pratiс╣гс╣нh├бy─Б.

[Pary─Бya III.тАФsaptakaс╕е. mantroktadevatyam. 50. ─Бsury anuс╣гс╣нubh; 51.
─Бrcy uс╣гс╣Зih; 52. 3-p. bhurik s─Бmn─л triс╣гс╣нubh; 53. ─Бsur─л bс╣Ыhat─л; 54. 2-p.
bhurik s─Бmn─л bс╣Ыhat─л; 55. s─Бmny uс╣гс╣Зih; 56. pr─Бj─Бpaty─Б bс╣Ыhat─л.]

Griffith

And thence, etc. . . . with other basis . . . Without standing-ground and resting-place thou wilt die . . . Having taken my stand on truth. With this I ate it, with this I came to it. Now this Odana is complete with all members, joints, and body. Complete, verily, with all his members, joints, and body is he who possesses this knowledge.
